  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ea6eb987-5bb2-47a8-a0fc-eb147e1bdb78'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText15339878792482859986" style="display:none"><i>Moxie girls fight back!</i><br /><br />Vivian Carter is fed up. Fed up with her small-town Texas high school that thinks the football team can do no wrong. Fed up with sexist dress codes and hallway harassment. But most of all, Viv Carter is fed up with always following the rules.<br /><br />Viv’s mom was a punk rock Riot Grrrl in the ’90s, so now Viv takes a page from her mother’s past and creates a feminist zine that she distributes anonymously to her classmates. She’s just blowing off steam, but other girls respond. Pretty soon Viv is forging friendships with other young women across the divides of cliques and popularity rankings, and she realizes that what she has started is nothing short of a girl revolution.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2038240407?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038240407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6232884747613109902">I’m going to be very transparent in the fact that I am never going to stop obsessing over this book. So be prepared, especially in the coming months of <i>Moxie</i>’s release, I ain’t shutting up about it.<br/><br/>I absolutely LOVED this book, way more than I anticipated. I originally wasn’t sure when I’d get to it, it just wasn’t high on my TBR, but after a sexist review, I knew I had to make it a priority and boy, did I make the right decision.<br/><br/>I do want to place a content warning for sexual harassment and tal</span>
  <span id="freeText6232884747613109902" style="display:none">I’m going to be very transparent in the fact that I am never going to stop obsessing over this book. So be prepared, especially in the coming months of <i>Moxie</i>’s release, I ain’t shutting up about it.<br /><br />I absolutely LOVED this book, way more than I anticipated. I originally wasn’t sure when I’d get to it, it just wasn’t high on my TBR, but after a sexist review, I knew I had to make it a priority and boy, did I make the right decision.<br /><br />I do want to place a content warning for sexual harassment and talk of rape/sexual assault (meaning we don’t necessarily see these events unfold like the sexual harassment spread throughout the book, but I still think it warrants a disclaimer that these sensitive topics are being discussed.)<br /><br /><i>Moxie</i> is a book that all teens and young adults NEED to read. It should be discussed in academia, it is an extremely important book. I especially want to recommend it to teens looking for empowerment and encouragement to share their voice. This book is getting a lot of hype for being a “feminist YA novel” and while it is entirely true that this is prime feminist literature for teens, I think the ultimate take away is that your voice, no matter how small, no matter how many people you stand against or how powerless you may feel, your voice is stronger. And I think everyone can use that reminder.<br /><br />I really loved Viv as a main character. I think she’s a very realistic and grounded character. She’s a fighter, she’s passionate, she always stands her ground on a topic she has feelings on, but she also deals with the insecurities of having friends that may not totally agree with you and not wanting to be labeled as someone who creates problems or goes against the group. She is articulate in her arguments, always able to get her point across in a non-patronizing, elegant way (I could learn a thing or two from her). I think she’s someone a lot of readers can look up to and strive towards. She definitely is fit to lead this feminist revolution at East Rockport High.<br /><br />I also really enjoyed Seth, who is the new boy and love interest in this novel (I didn’t originally expect there to be a romance, but it is a very small part of the story and definitely does not overtake the main message.) Seth is a very understanding person, always willing to listen and do better. I think he and Viv have one of the healthiest YA relationships because even though they may argue and unintentionally hurt the other, they are willing to talk it out and do better in the future. Seth learns about Viv’s efforts to change the sexism in her school early on, and he really cares that it’s something she is passionate about! He definitely has his slip ups where he just doesn’t understand due to not experiencing the sexism that the girls in his classes have, but when Viv takes the time to explain, *he listens and learns.* This book definitely tackles male privilege and I wouldn’t be surprised if some of my reading friends who are men are uncomfortable while reading this, but I think that’s why it’s so beneficial to a variety of populations. One of my favorite scenes is when Viv wants to help spread “Moxie” to the boys in their school, but he is actually the one to suggest that it should be a space just for girls, and he understands fully when Viv confirms it (<b>Yes, Kirkus reviews, I AM looking dead at your for spreading a false narrative of men being excluded from the feminist efforts in this story, especially since they are important figures in this movement by the end.</b>) In my opinion, Seth is a really good guy focused on learning more about other’s experiences<br /><br />Of course, my favorite part of this novel was ALL THE FEMINISM. This book is full of girls supporting girls, girls of different cliques coming together for the same goals, girls learning more about what it means to be a feminist and why it is important to stand with each other instead of against. In saying this, I’m not trying to suggest that feminism is “only for women” (which I discuss below) but I’m so happy to have a novel of girls working with other girls that readers can look up to. Despite all the sexism and harassment in the book, I got nothing but fluffy feels from all the “Moxie” activities going on like tackling unfair dress codes, bake sales and art sales to raise funds for girls sports, and just generally seeing the spark ignite within all these teens. <br /><br />I am also pleased that this book does tackle the privilege of white women regarding feminist issues. We do have a few POC who play a role in this movement (I think one is black and one is latinx if I am remembering correctly) and they definitely explain to Viv how even though she is experiencing sexism like them, it’s entirely different for her being a white girl. I really appreciate the efforts to make the distinction of how some women are at a greater disadvantage within the general sexism of society.<br /><br />If you couldn’t tell, I loved this book. It is a fast-paced, CRUCIAL read that I hope you all give a chance. When I get some extra cash, I definitely will be giving away some pre-orders because I want this book in your hands *that* much. I’d highly highly recommend it to readers of all ages who are looking to be represented, looking to learn, or looking to be empowered. I honestly feel this book has the power to change lives, and I know it has left an impact on mine. <i>Moxie</i> is out September 19th, so please either pre-order it or reserve it at your local library!<br /><br /><i> I received a copy of this book for free from Macmillan at Book Expo 2017. I had no&gt; obligation to review this book and all opinions are my own.</i></span>

<div id="review_1857598683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1857598683" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1857598683?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone looking for a fun feminist contemporary</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2017">y-out2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=she-did-that">she-did-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-arcs">x-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1857598683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16790425713265382036">In light of Kirkus' gross review of this, an added paragraph. <b>I do not at all agree that this book “drives away male allies.”</b> Given the content of the book Kirkus was referring to, I am of the opinion that this is a really gross opinion. <b>If you think “calling out a person who's victim-blaming a rape survivor” is the same as “driving away male allies”, please consider blocking me.</b> <br/><br/>This isn't even an <i>accurate</i> concern. The dude we're referring too, the main character's boyfriend, is given a chance </span>
  <span id="freeText16790425713265382036" style="display:none">In light of Kirkus' gross review of this, an added paragraph. <b>I do not at all agree that this book “drives away male allies.”</b> Given the content of the book Kirkus was referring to, I am of the opinion that this is a really gross opinion. <b>If you think “calling out a person who's victim-blaming a rape survivor” is the same as “driving away male allies”, please consider blocking me.</b> <br /><br />This isn't even an <i>accurate</i> concern. The dude we're referring too, the main character's boyfriend, is given a chance to learn from his gross comments and begin working through his own misogyny. God, I don't even know if I would've given someone a chance to redeem themselves from some of the things said in this book. No, the main character does not consider it acceptable that <b>her boyfriend implies rape is the victim's fault.</b> You know why she's not okay with that? Because it's a gross belief and it's not one anyone should accept in a boyfriend. <br /><br />I'm trying to be sympathetic to other opinions here, but Kirkus' review is not a different opinion on a book or a different viewpoint on how feminism works. <b>It's an ideology, and it's a fucking terrible one.</b> It is perfectly acceptable to dislike this book - we all like and dislike stuff - but the fact that you don't give a shit about rape victims, whether they be men <i>or</i> women, isn't one of them. Thanks. <br /><br /><br /><b>WE'RE DONE WITH THE SEXIST BULLSHIT - LET'S REVIEW</b><br /><br />Okay, basic premise: A bunch of girls join together to protest sexism at their school. The book starts out without a ton of character depth, with the obvious feminist girl and the obvious naysayer girl and the obvious boyfriend. <b>The book proceeds to smack down all of your expectations for how this is going to play out.</b> The best friend isn't vilified for not starting out as an ardent feminist. The boyfriend's occasional problematic actions are called out in a really healthy way. Even the obvious popular girl who loves dating and guys gets a character arc and isn't slutshamed. <br /><br />I kind of love how unapologetically feminist this book is. The author touches on a lot of different feminist topics, and even mentions how those topics intersect with lgbt issues and with racism. I was expecting the book to be very one-dimensional dealing with those topics. But this book was better than that. <b>There are characters who do sexist things despite trying their best, other characters <i>call them out</i>, and they grow and change.</b> Yay for second chances and character development. I have to say, <b>I would've appreciate a <i>bit</i> more actual intersectionality, rather than characters just talking about it</b>. But in general, that aspect of the book was great. <br /><br />Aside from discussing the basic premise and etc etc etc, everything about this is solid contemporary material. The characters are well-drawn with good arcs, although none of them resonated with me in any particular way. The romance is sweet, the plot is interesting, the writing is quite compelling... I don't have anything amazing to say and I don't have anything particularly bad to say. What made this book stand out to me was the interesting and <b>non-stereotypical</b> dialogue around feminism. <br /><br />I would like to add a trigger warning for a lot of gross things being said about rape victims, which are called out, obviously. <br /><br />Do you want to read this yet? Because I loved it, and I hope everyone else will too. And of course, if you get an arc of this please check the blurbs on page one, because I'm quoted!!<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=netgalley-all">netgalley-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2112610232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18363072803415224701"><b>UPDATE: $2.99 on kindle US today 6/27/20</b><br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504465191i/23760607._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book was totally amazing! I was in tears near the end with all of the girls standing up together. They were there for each other, girls from all walks of life to stand up against those that try to make them something they are not, for trying to push them into corners to go along with things that shouldn't be. This book is all powerful in its own way. <br/><br/>Viv is a girl that goes to high school like your normal teen. She lives with her mom, her dad died whe</span>
  <span id="freeText18363072803415224701" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE: $2.99 on kindle US today 6/27/20</b><br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504465191i/23760607._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was totally amazing! I was in tears near the end with all of the girls standing up together. They were there for each other, girls from all walks of life to stand up against those that try to make them something they are not, for trying to push them into corners to go along with things that shouldn't be. This book is all powerful in its own way. <br><br>Viv is a girl that goes to high school like your normal teen. She lives with her mom, her dad died when she was young, her grandparents live next door, she has friends, life is pretty okay. Not so much at school. The school is run by the star football players and they get away with everything. Mitchell Wilson is the leader of the pack and his father is the Principle of the school, so he gets away with even more. The football team gets all the money while other parts of the school are in the dark ages. <br><br>But one day, Viv has had enough. When a new girl named Lucy is trying to answer a question in class and Mitchell makes a comment that sends Viv on a quest to end this crap. <br><br>Viv gets the idea to start a zine called Moxie from reading through her moms old stuff in a box. Her mom was pretty hard core when she was younger. <br><br>Viv designs pages and makes copies of them and puts them in the girls bathrooms. There are some cool pictures in the book but I won't share them until I get my physical copy when it comes out in case something changes. <br><br>Moxie slowly starts a revolution. A revolution of girls to not be shamed, or groped, or raped, or pushed to the side. This movement causes girls that would have never talked to each other to be friends and to stick up for one another. They even do bake sales and stuff so the girls soccer team can have new uniforms. It's so freaking uplifting that all I can say is read the book and find out for yourselves. <br><br>The idea of girls coming together as friends and not being jealous or petty is fantastic! <br><br>And in this small town having a movement like this and going against the higher ups in the school is something everyone should do if they are living in a corrupt area. A principle pushing attempted rape and other things aside like they are nothing is not something that needs to let go by the wayside. <br><br>The book made me feel good inside. And the author left some websites for people to look at for different groups. I love it! <br><br>There is also a love interest for Viv in the book. His name is Seth and even though some don't think this should be a book for romance I have to disagree. I loved Seth and I think the placement of a hot high school guy that doesn't think like the jerks was a great thing. It didn't take away from the book, it was just there along with the other norms of life. <br><br>Mel ♥<br><br>*Thank you to Netgalley and the publisher for giving me the opportunity to read this book.*<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/09/moxie-by-jennifer-mathieu.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_2043770025" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2043770025" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2043770025?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2043770025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12578974552599349288">Not long ago, I wrote an essay on the importance of feminism to various groups of people today and presented it to the class. The response was overwhelmingly positive and sparked different discussions. <br/><br/>The teacher was surprised. He looked at me and said, ‘‘This is how every oral presentation should go.’’ But then immediately after, as if really thinking about the issues I presented, he asked, ‘‘But are you girls, at your age, really affected by unfeminist behaviours?’’<br/><br/>The girls of our class (the</span>
  <span id="freeText12578974552599349288" style="display:none">Not long ago, I wrote an essay on the importance of feminism to various groups of people today and presented it to the class. The response was overwhelmingly positive and sparked different discussions. <br /><br />The teacher was surprised. He looked at me and said, ‘‘This is how every oral presentation should go.’’ But then immediately after, as if really thinking about the issues I presented, he asked, ‘‘But are you girls, at your age, really affected by unfeminist behaviours?’’<br /><br />The girls of our class (there were only two boys), myself included, were speechless for a second, and then a girl spoke up. ‘‘Well, we’re girls, so of course we’re affected by sexism,’’ she said and I could have applauded her for it. Perfect answer. <br /><br />My teacher was not sexist, but he was not a woman. His question proves that there is much he doesn’t understand about the hundred ways in which men can be sexist towards women. MOXIE is a book he should read. <br /><br />MOXIE is a book everyone should read. Just like THE HATE U GIVE, another fiction story full of powerful, revolutionary themes that feels all too real, it is important, revealing, poignant and extremely touching. <br /><br />I have an issue with it, however. While Vivian grows a lot, throughout the novel—she gain courage, strength and determination—there still seems to be stereotypical thinking she condones that she isn’t aware of, for instance, waiting for the guy to kiss the girl first (isn’t feminism about empowering women?) and wanting to go out with a guy taller than she is (come on, we must get rid of this thinking that men should always be taller!). <br /><br />It could have had more dept also, but it’s a very good feminist YA novel. There should be more books like this one. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12578974552599349288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2055888514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2055888514" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2055888514?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=contemporaries">contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=deserves-the-hype">deserves-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2055888514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4075412605789157612"><b> 4 Stars </b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> “…a feminist. It’s not a bad word. After today it might be my favorite word. Because really all it is is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that’s always finding ways to tell them they’re not.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Okay, I’ll admit it. I was <i>so</i> nervous about reading this. I absolutely consider myself a feminist, but I also think <b>writing a fiction book about a political/social movement is tricky.</b> It’s very easy to lose focus on the characters and story—or e</span>
  <span id="freeText4075412605789157612" style="display:none"><b> 4 Stars </b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “…a feminist. It’s not a bad word. After today it might be my favorite word. Because really all it is is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that’s always finding ways to tell them they’re not.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Okay, I’ll admit it. I was <i>so</i> nervous about reading this. I absolutely consider myself a feminist, but I also think <b>writing a fiction book about a political/social movement is tricky.</b> It’s very easy to lose focus on the characters and story—or even worse, end up with a bunch of weak, stereotypes that exist only to promote the primary message. <br /><br /><i>Not</i> the case here. <br /><br />The character’s aren’t just a teaching tool to talk about feminism. <b>Feminism is a teaching tool for the characters.</b> Our MC, Vivian, has a fully-formed character arc that works in conjunction with the plot as she ‘accidentally’ starts a feminist club at her school. It all worked very well together to give us an <i>awesome</i> story about change and revolution. <br /><br />Speaking of, <i>none</i> of the characters were stereotypes. <b>Nothing was condensed down to black-or-white.</b> The character’s weren’t divided into ‘good feminist’ and some ‘bad other,’ but instead, allowed to be flawed and dynamic—just like real people. Vivian’s best-friend has reservations about using the word feminism, Vivian’s love interest (who self-identifies as a feminist) still holds some problematic views—Vivian herself makes judgments and holds opinions that are questionable, and discussed as she matures. <b>There was more focus on growth, than shaming anyone.</b><br /><br />Female friendship is <i>still</i> all too rare in YA, and this book has it in <i>spades.</i> Each chapter is filled with <b>girls supporting, laughing, debating, and learning from each-other.</b> I especially appreciated how Vivian’s friendship with Claudia wasn’t dismissed just because she also befriends the new girl, Lucie. Girls of different races, orientations, classes and walks-of-life not only work together, but <i>revel</i> in their friendships. <br /><br />My only complaint is that as much as I loved the story, I couldn’t help but feel <b>the writing was a little bland.</b> There was a complete lack of sensory details, and all the descriptions were pretty plain. I understand the story and characters were the front of the story, but I wouldn’t have minded a little <i>more oomph</i> to draw me in, ya know? <br /><br />Also, it’s not that ‘make-me-a-sandwich’ jokes are rare (god help us) but there’s an instance where a boy interrupts a girl <i>just</i> to say the punchline? It didn’t feel very organic, and felt even more off in a book so grounded in realism. <br /><br /><b> In Conclusion </b><br /><br /> Really fun, really empowering contemporary where the character’s and their relationships are the focus to open awesome discussions about feminism. Some of my <b>favorite quotes:</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “I’ve never thought about it like that. That a white girl always wins.”<br />“Well no offense,” sas Kiera, eyeing me, “but you’re white, so you wouldn't have.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “And you telling me not all guys are like that doesn’t really help me feel better. Because some guys <u>are</u> like that. A lot of them, actually.”</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “Making girls monitor their behavior and their appearance because boys are supposedly unable to control themselves? That is one of the oldest fucking tricks in the book.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “It’s like I’m living in a feminist fantasy,” Lucy says. “But it can’t be a complete fantasy, because Roxane Gay isn’t here.”</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br />Anyway, this review is like 34 years late, but this was a buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/68157476-may" rel="nofollow noopener">the one who doesn't appreciate my mango jokes.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4075412605789157612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2029857722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2029857722" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2029857722?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2029857722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16294127464660185601"><b>"This is what it means to be a feminist. Not a humanist or an equalist or whatever. But a feminist. It's not a bad word. After today it might be my favorite word. Because really all it is is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that's always finding ways to tell them they're not."</b> <br/><br/>A book about a teen girl coming into her own as a feminist and learning how to fight back against the patriarchy and rape culture? ... do you think I could have clicked "re</span>
  <span id="freeText16294127464660185601" style="display:none"><b>"This is what it means to be a feminist. Not a humanist or an equalist or whatever. But a feminist. It's not a bad word. After today it might be my favorite word. Because really all it is is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that's always finding ways to tell them they're not."</b> <br /><br />A book about a teen girl coming into her own as a feminist and learning how to fight back against the patriarchy and rape culture? ... do you think I could have clicked "request" on this ARC any faster than I did?<br /><br /><b>✘ PLOT</b><br />At Vivian's high school, she's used to certain things being fact: the football players get away with everything, dress codes only affect girls, and sexual harassment is just part of everyday life. When Vivian starts to delve into her mother's Riot Grrrl past, however, she realizes maybe things don't have to be this way - so she forms Moxie, an anonymous school 'zine that invites other girls to band together and fight back.<br /><br /><b>"Riot Grrrls were into feminism, obviously, but up until this moment in the gym I didn't think of them as feminists so much as super cool girls who took no shit."</b><br /><br /><b>✘ WHAT I LIKED</b><br />- This is, in a nutshell, a YA contemporary about feminism, and that's a topic that most authors aren't willing to touch with a ten-foot pole. Not only does Jennifer Mathieu tackle the issue, she does it with finesse and smoothness.<br /><br />- <b>INTERSECTIONALITY!</b> Vivian is given a firsthand lesson in the problematic aspects of "white feminism" and learns how to take the extra steps needed to ensure complete inclusion of <i>all</i> women (not just the white girls).<br /><br />- <b>Growth and development</b>. When we first start the story, Vivian has a few problematic views on things, but she is open to listening and learning. There are even a few times where she admits to bristling a little over things she is taught, but she quickly puts her knee-jerk reactions aside and <i>listens</i>.<br /><br />We also watch several other characters grow a <i>lot</i> - as in the case with Viv's best friend, who turns her nose up at the thought of feminism in the beginning of the book, but as she learns more about the movement, she steadily becomes more open-minded until she is finally proud to call herself a feminist, too.<br /><br />- When Viv first starts creating the Moxie 'zines and working towards dismantling the school's patriarchal system, she's so gung-ho about it that she tends to fly off the handle whenever anyone says anything incorrect. I think a <i>lot</i> of feminists have been in her shoes (I know I have, and it took me a few years to learn that I don't have to get <i>angry</i> at every person who hasn't been educated).<br /><br />While the book doesn't promote turning the other cheek regarding people who willfully ignore sexism (or any other relevant -ism), it does promote <b>giving people the chance to learn and grow</b>, and that is so important! Rome wasn't built in a day, guys, and you can't undo a lifetime of indoctrination in one conversation, but when people are making an <i>effort</i> to learn, the most helpful thing we can do is give them a healthy chance.<br /><br />- <i>Moxie</i> addresses <b>rape culture</b> head on. So many people don't realize how many ways rape culture affects our day-to-day lives, and I was delighted to watch Vivian not only come to realize how much it affected her and her friends, but to watch her fight back against it. There's even an aspect where she touches on the fact that men, regardless of their stance on feminism, <i>cannot fully comprehend what women go through</i>, and I swear, I almost put the book down to <b>applaud</b> Jennifer Mathieu for having the guts to go there.<br /><br /><b>"I'm totally sure he's not doing it on purpose, but Seth is a guy, and he can't ever know what it feels like to walk down a hallway and know that you're getting judged for the size of your ass or how big your boobs are. He'll never understand what it's like to second guess everything you wear and how you sit and walk and stand in case it doesn't attract the right kind of attention or worse, attracts the wrong kind. <i>He'll never get how scary and crazy-making it is to feel like you belong to some big Boy Monster that decides it can grab you and touch you and rank you whenever and however it wants.</i>"</b><br /><br /><b>✘ WHAT I DIDN'T LIKE</b><br />My only complaint about this book - and the reason I gave it 4 stars instead of 5 - is that the story itself relies so heavily on the feminist aspect that the parts in between, where we're just focusing on Viv's daily life, friendships, romance, etc., fall short a little. The writing felt very young at times, and I actually had to remind myself several times that Viv was a junior in high school, because a lot of her wording and inner monologues just felt more like they were coming from a 14- or 15-year-old, at most.<br /><br /><b>✘ FINAL VERDICT</b><br />Is this book flawless <i>as a contemporary</i>? No. It's a little mediocre on the <i>story-telling</i> aspect. Is this book a brilliant and fun example of what feminism is intended to be, however? Absolutely! Whether you consider yourself a feminist or not, I feel like everyone could learn something from this book - and you might even be surprised by how hard some of the quotes hit home.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to NetGalley and Roaring Brook Press for the ARC! All opinions expressed in this review are entirely my own.</i><br /><br />You can also find this review on my blog <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2017/08/21/moxie/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16294127464660185601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2526690988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2526690988" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2526690988?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">actual young teens or middle schoolers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2">2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=starred-2017">starred-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2018">2018</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2526690988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer190094928294208809">A little quiz.<br/><br/>1) A guy who repeatedly yells to you "Make me a sandwich!" and wears a t-shirt with the words "Nice legs, when do they open"? is:<br/><br/>a) bad<br/>b) good<br/>c) I don't know<br/><br/>2) Who should be punished for breaking school dress code: a girl who wears a scoop-neck shirt or a guy who wears a t-shirt with a big arrow pointing to bellow his waist and words "Free Breathalyzer Test Blow Here"?<br/><br/>a) boy<br/>b) girl<br/>c) I don't know<br/><br/>3) What should a high school principal do when a girl reports being sexually assaulted </span>
  <span id="freeText190094928294208809" style="display:none">A little quiz.<br /><br />1) A guy who repeatedly yells to you "Make me a sandwich!" and wears a t-shirt with the words "Nice legs, when do they open"? is:<br /><br />a) bad<br />b) good<br />c) I don't know<br /><br />2) Who should be punished for breaking school dress code: a girl who wears a scoop-neck shirt or a guy who wears a t-shirt with a big arrow pointing to bellow his waist and words "Free Breathalyzer Test Blow Here"?<br /><br />a) boy<br />b) girl<br />c) I don't know<br /><br />3) What should a high school principal do when a girl reports being sexually assaulted by a boy in a school hallway?<br /><br />a) take this issue very seriously, investigate thoroughly and punish the boy accordingly<br />b) tell the girl to take it as a compliment and move on with her life<br />c) I don't know.<br /><br />If you've answered b) or c) to any of these questions, "Moxie" is the book for you. Otherwise, you may be too old to read it. <br /><br />I don't want to knock it, but this novel has very little adult crossover appeal, IMO. It's the most basic feminist YA story and may educate a 12-year old who is not yet weary of bluntness and absence of nuance. <br /><br />P.S. Reasonable adults are nowhere to be seen in this narrative. Again.</span>

<div id="review_2095440337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2095440337" />
    <a title="Taneika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika"><img alt="Taneika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564410672p2/5591031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2095440337?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taneika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taneika" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika">Taneika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444940633" href="/book/show/35383830-moxie">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2095440337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2447751106470880577">4.5/5 stars!<br/><br/>I want to make it clear that I LOVED THIS BOOK SO SO MUCH. <br/><br/>Moxie is about Vivian, who is sick of the sexist shit that goes down at her high school and feeling inspired by her mum's 90's Riot Grrrl feminist zines, decides to make her own feminist zine to fight against the patriarchy and stand up for girls.<br/><br/>As a character, Viv is a bit shy, quiet and is scared of speaking out and getting caught making these zines in the first place. While she is quiet and a bit scared at first, she is a</span>
  <span id="freeText2447751106470880577" style="display:none">4.5/5 stars!<br /><br />I want to make it clear that I LOVED THIS BOOK SO SO MUCH. <br /><br />Moxie is about Vivian, who is sick of the sexist shit that goes down at her high school and feeling inspired by her mum's 90's Riot Grrrl feminist zines, decides to make her own feminist zine to fight against the patriarchy and stand up for girls.<br /><br />As a character, Viv is a bit shy, quiet and is scared of speaking out and getting caught making these zines in the first place. While she is quiet and a bit scared at first, she is also passionate and super realistic! In her journey of creating these zines and accidentally starting a movement, she comes across many people, including those who are close to her, who aren't necessarily on board with what she's doing (or what the "creator of Moxie" is doing). Viv doesn't want to be labelled as somebody who is different or as somebody who stands out, but she still fights for what she believes in which is something I absolutely adored. <br />Viv's relationship with her mum was SO-FREAKING-CUTE-I-LOVED-IT. It was SUCH a relief to see a protagonist who has a close relationship with their mother, and seeing their relationship throughout the novel was definitely one of my favourite aspects.<br /><br />There is a tiny bit of romance in this book and Viv's boyfriend Seth is understanding, willing to learn and learning to work through things he doesn't quite understand as he doesn't know what it's like to be a girl. Whenever Seth slips up, Viv is quick to talk things out with him and he ACTUALLY LISTENS. He's such a good ally to the girls, and it was a joy to read about. My only gripe (and it's not even really a gripe), is that I also thought their relationship was a little unnecessary. While it didn't take away from the story or the themes, I felt like Seth was almost entirely used as a plot device to explain certain things about feminism. I think Seth as a boyfriend, could have easily been replaced with Seth as a best friend or Seth as a friend, and it would've had the same effect. <br /><br />Naturally, my favourite part of this book was ALL THE FEMINISM. I found myself cheering Viv and the others on, I found myself getting angry (SO ANGRY) but overall I felt so empowered. Moxie honestly bought me back to when I first started learning what it means to be a feminist and I almost want to cry just thinking about how this might teach young people in school what it means to be a feminist and that it might encourage them to branch out and research more. <br />Moxie addresses things like dress code (which thankfully, isn't a HUGE thing in Australian public schools as most schools have a uniform), the "not all men" attitude and rape culture which was SO INCREDIBLY EXECUTED OMG.<br /><br />While Moxie does have a few diverse characters (there is one black girl, a latina girl and we very briefly learn there are two closeted girls who like girls), I kind of wish there was a bit more intersectionationality. While the author talks about this in the Author Note and while the text does touch on intersectional feminism:<br /><br /><i>"The night we watched that documentary about Kathleen Hanna, my mom talked about how Riot Grrrl was mostly white girls, and she was sorry they weren't as welcoming to other girls as they could've been. That it was one of the few regrets she had about the whole thing. But that was as far as she'd gone. East Rockport High isn't just white girls, for sure. I glance over where Kiera and Amaya are sitting. I think about how in this one way, maybe Moxie could be even better than the Riot Grrrls. Even stronger"</i><br /><br />I think the author did a good job of discussing it, but I think it just needed to be more present throughout the book to really push the important message across. <br /><br />Despite having a few minor issues with side character development/depth and showing intersectionality in the text, I absolutely adored Moxie. The feminist issues it addressed were tackled brilliantly, Viv is an amazing and realistic protagonist, I loved the relationships and most of all I love the girl power. There was NO girl hate in this, even with different cliques in highschool, and I was living for it.<br /><br />Definitely a must-read for girls, guys and non binary pals. Even if you learn nothing new about feminism after reading Moxie, at the very least, it'll make you happy, angry and feel empowered all at once.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2447751106470880577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2063638258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2063638258" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2063638258?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2063638258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13763984441229660141">This book was so touching. I love the fire and passion of all the characters about justice, and I think it's such an important narrative. The fact that the love interest identified as a feminist was enough to bring tears to my eyes. And I also love how this touches on the fact that feminism isn't perfect and people who try to help still makes mistakes. I wish 16 year old me could have read this and been inspired, so it's my only hope that girls that age will really internalize this.<br/><br/>My only two c</span>
  <span id="freeText13763984441229660141" style="display:none">This book was so touching. I love the fire and passion of all the characters about justice, and I think it's such an important narrative. The fact that the love interest identified as a feminist was enough to bring tears to my eyes. And I also love how this touches on the fact that feminism isn't perfect and people who try to help still makes mistakes. I wish 16 year old me could have read this and been inspired, so it's my only hope that girls that age will really internalize this.<br /><br />My only two complaints were only minor hindrances to my reading experience. Firstly, the word "totally" is overused to a noticable and embarrassing degree. Secondly, this requires a bit of suspension of disbelief. I went to school in conservative Texas where strict dress codes are upheld and boys make nasty comments, but some parts of this just seemed over the edge unrealistic. Sometimes it was the boys being able to get away with obviously crude things, and sometimes it was the girls' reactions to it. I hate to say it, but I think this reads a bit like an idealized version of how a perfect world would fight back and treat sexists. In reality, I couldn't envision this many girls realistically rallying behind the purpose of Moxie, especially in the conversative south. That being said, I like how enthusiastically and passionate these girls were portrayed, even though it nagged at me that I couldn't see anything similar happening in my school or anywhere near me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13763984441229660141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10717338185738378954" style="display:none">first half of this book: boring boring boring contemporary boring high school boring everything boring meh<br /><br />second half of this book: FEMINIST CITY INTERSECTIONAL GLORY GIRLS BEING GIRLS TOGETHER AND BRINGING EACH OTHER UP FOR LIFE I LOVE IT <s>and also a fair bit more making out than is my ideal</s><br /><br />Basically, if I could delete the first 150 pages of this and also the entire romance subplot from the whole thing, this would be a five star read. So as is, it's not perfect for me.<br /><br />What is perfect are two final scenes that I will put in spoiler tags here so I can yell about them without anyone yelling at me:<br />1) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when they have the Moxie party in the hall and it's just girls being girls together with no boys in sight. I want to hang out with a lot of girls and have no boys be there. That has literally never happened to me in my life <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />2) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[THAT WALKOUT SCENE BOIIIII like oh my god I felt EMPOWERED I felt STRESSED I felt ready to SCREAM and SHOUT and WALK OUT OF PUBLIC EDUCATION BUILDINGS. I would have to walk into one in order to walk out of one, which wasn't on my short list of things to ever do again for the rest of my life, but I'd do it for the squad. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Unfortunately, while I loved those two (2) moments a whole lot, I really didn't like a lot of other stuff. Like that STUPID ROMANCE and how BORING AND SLOW most of it was. Like, if you're writing a feminist book and it takes a while to get to the feminist part......maybe speed it up.<br /><br />So this wasn't a perfect book for me. But it did have perfect parts!!!<br /><br />Bottom line: Life is complicated!! Also, yay feminism!!!!<br /><br />------------------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />list of things i need right now:<br /><br />1) a good dose of feminism<br />2) to sleep for a hundred hours<br />3) see number one</span>

<div id="review_2146713532" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2146713532" />
    <a title="Joce (squibblesreads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48087215-joce-squibblesreads"><img alt="Joce (squibblesreads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445310967p2/48087215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2146713532?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joce (squibblesreads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joce (squibblesreads)" href="/user/show/48087215-joce-squibblesreads">Joce (squibblesreads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2146713532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16813697175075524981">3.75 stars (maybe 3.5 if I decide to weigh the issue I speak about more heavily)<br/>I enjoyed this, and I wish there'd been more books like this when I was a teen!<br/>My favorite parts were the shoutout to Roxane Gay (woohoo!), the depiction of the small town, and the portrayal of the different ways the adult men at the school were particularly shitty and how the power dynamic played into it. I also loved how Viv's relationship with her mom wasn't necessarily perfect, and that some things were out of he</span>
  <span id="freeText16813697175075524981" style="display:none">3.75 stars (maybe 3.5 if I decide to weigh the issue I speak about more heavily)<br />I enjoyed this, and I wish there'd been more books like this when I was a teen!<br />My favorite parts were the shoutout to Roxane Gay (woohoo!), the depiction of the small town, and the portrayal of the different ways the adult men at the school were particularly shitty and how the power dynamic played into it. I also loved how Viv's relationship with her mom wasn't necessarily perfect, and that some things were out of her control, and how that affected her. Lucy is also a badass, and I'd love to have been a Lucy when I was in high school.<br />The critique I have is that even though I know it was set in a small town and there may not be much diversity in the population to begin with, there were some POC side characters that had very obvious "side character" roles, and I am pretty sure the protag is an allo cis het Caucasian girl. I would have loved for this story to center on a girl who was not entirely of the dominant discourse, and some more inclusion, particularly mention of disability, neurodiversity, gender identity, and sexuality.<br />The author mentioned that she wanted Moxie to be more inclusive than Riot Grrls, and mentioned intersectional feminism in her afterword and acknowledgements, so I know it is important to her and she is aware of it, but that inclusion would have been great to see within the book itself.<br />It seemed like the feminist issues discussed in the book were ONLY about gender, and not about the different ways that gender can interact with race, sexuality, disability, neurodiversity, etc. So while it did acknowledge the presence and weight of intersectionality, it did not incorporate it as much as necessary, or at all. There is never any situation where gender exists in a vacuum the way it seemed like it did in this book. Including POC as an entity by itself does not make the addressing of feminist issues intersectional at all; in fact I would argue that this engages in some erasure (albeit probably unintentionally) and was unsatisfying. I saw a quote once that asked “if feminism is not intersectional, is it really feminism?” and that is definitely a question I was asking for the duration of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16813697175075524981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8522774633476489237"><b>Moxie Girls Fight Back!</b> ALL OF THE STARS FOR YOU!<br/><br/><i>Really all it is, is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that's finding ways to tell them they're not.</i><br/><br/><b>Trigger Warning: Sexual Assault</b><br/><br/>If I could just stand up and applaud this book. IT IS AMAZING. In the last 30 pages I could of cried at just how proud I am of all the girls (and some boys) at the awful awful school! I can safely say that I identify as a Feminist, and sometimes this word can be seen as </span>
  <span id="freeText8522774633476489237" style="display:none"><b>Moxie Girls Fight Back!</b> ALL OF THE STARS FOR YOU!<br /><br /><i>Really all it is, is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that's finding ways to tell them they're not.</i><br /><br /><b>Trigger Warning: Sexual Assault</b><br /><br />If I could just stand up and applaud this book. IT IS AMAZING. In the last 30 pages I could of cried at just how proud I am of all the girls (and some boys) at the awful awful school! I can safely say that I identify as a Feminist, and sometimes this word can be seen as something entirely different to what it is... <i>which isn't the case</i>. It's not about hating men, it's simply being seen as an equal. I think what was so well done is that it wasn't just about this, but the issue of race representation was brought into this... and I LOVED it. It's so refreshing to see actual girl power, and all uniting. There's no bitchyness it's just them all coming together for something they believe in!<br /><br /><b>Vivian</b> is our leading lady, she's such a strong character! We see her beginning to question how things are done at her school when the guys on the football team seem to get away with anything they want. It's like come on now! We see her grow from strength to strength. We see how she can be insecure and not always able to voice her opinion, however we see her fight for what she believes in and how passionate she is with this. It was one of those moments I was literally like "you go girl!". She's everything I want in one of my leading ladies!<br /><br />Special shout out to <i>Lucy</i>, I can't get over how much I loved her character. I honestly can't. She was <u>so</u> strong willed and so passionate about everything, trying to bring in things from her previous school, how she was so happy to help other people. She also pointed out issues with race and stood her ground to help other people.<br /><br />We also have <b>Seth</b>, the love interest of Vivian. Now I know he's not perfect. HOWEVER he actually <u>learns</u> and with that that he understands things that he may not have known before. He offers his support and is understanding of WHY it's important!<br /><br />What I <b>liked?</b><br />- I really liked Vivians Meemaw and Grandpa, I know they were set in there ways, but it was honestly so relatable to my nana and grandad, it was just so cute!<br />- Vivians mum is all for Girl Power!<br />- <b>ALL OF THE FEMINISM!</b><br />- The zines we got to see<br />- Just how it actually made me feel, I could feel myself getting riled up, and you know you care about something when a book makes you want to step in the pages and have your own say on things.<br /><br />What I <b>didn't like?</b><br />- The fucking headteacher and his son, "take it as a compliment" my arseeeee!<br />(but this is also key to the story, just me getting het up)<br /><br />Overall I recommend this to anyone and everyone, it's books like this that NEED to be in schools. It makes it easier to talk about issues that people can face that are often just brushed off. I loved this so much, and I honestly think this book will stay with me for a long time!<br /><br /><b>I want to paint stars and hearts on my hand and be like MOXIE!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8522774633476489237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2146147504" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2146147504" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2146147504?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35445532-moxie">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young Teens learning about feminism for the first time</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emer (A Little Haze) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/55137572-aimee">Aimee</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=challenge-sum2018">challenge-sum2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2018">read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=2stars">2stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2146147504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16080557234717034181">I wasn't going to read Moxie. I got the vibe from it that it was sort of a book for the younger end of the YA spectrum and well... I'm a couple of decades past that *gulps*<br/><br/>But in my book group (currently recruiting new, interested members so hit me up for an invite 👍🏻)... Anyway we have this reading challenge this summer and basically we are all recommending different books to each other to read and discuss together. It's good fun! <br/><br/>So one of my friends in the group, Aimee *waves at Aimee* recomm</span>
  <span id="freeText16080557234717034181" style="display:none">I wasn't going to read Moxie. I got the vibe from it that it was sort of a book for the younger end of the YA spectrum and well... I'm a couple of decades past that *gulps*<br /><br />But in my book group (currently recruiting new, interested members so hit me up for an invite 👍🏻)... Anyway we have this reading challenge this summer and basically we are all recommending different books to each other to read and discuss together. It's good fun! <br /><br />So one of my friends in the group, Aimee *waves at Aimee* recommended Moxie and I thought... Eh they have this in my library, why not borrow and read it. I know... SUCH enthusiasm *cackles* <br /><br />Anywho.... You know that gut feeling you sometimes have about a book before you read it... Mine was definitely right this time. This is definitely a book for younger YA or for someone who knows very little about feminism and its true meaning. Basically this book is a teaching book. I remember flipping to the back page of the book and it revealing that the author is a teacher and I was like... Yup. That makes soooo much sense!!!<br /><br />Okay. It's not a bad book per se. It's just... Well it's entirely too heavy handed. There is a distinct lack of subtlety in the writing and there are simply too many feminist issues covered in the one book so that it begins to take on an almost too dramatised a persona...if books can have personas?? *shrugs* Case in point: the principal in the school is written in such a fashion that he becomes pantomime-esque. <br /><br />But there are some nice plus points. <br /><br />Genuine female friendships that have their ebbs and flows but overall are immensely empowering. So frequently in YA we get casual girl-girl hatred so it's lovely to see the interactions of the girls in this. I mean it's possibly too idealised with how buddy buddy everyone ultimately is but damn it, it's important to hammer home that message that as girls / women etc we should support each other and not knock each other down.<br /><br />We had some very one dimensional male villains who barely had any character descriptions about them but we were treated to a greyer leading male teenage character. I very much enjoyed his character arc and how it showed that no one's perfect but we can all learn. The same could be said about one of the female besties of the MC (although I would have liked her to learn in possibly a slightly different manner). But overall, characters that were not always correct in their viewpoints but still likeable, genuine etc. <br /><br />The MC Viv was a little bit of a letdown for me. I appreciated everything the author tried to do with her and she had the potential for great character motivations... But I felt I was told about many of these motivations rather than truly got any genuine feeling from her. She was a little bland and sometimes unnecessarily whiny especially regarding events surrounding her mother. The whininess could have been fine, because god knows we all like to whinge and moan and she had genuine reason for it... but the development of the storyline with her mother was ultimately wrapped up all too neat and tidily therefore making her whininess feel unreasonable and tiresome... Ergo. Poor writing. <br /><br />I really appreciated how the book got across the message about why it is we need feminism and that being feminist does not mean you are anti-men or doesn't mean that you don't believe in equal rights. I think there are some wonderfully eye opening paragraphs explaining the feminist movement that would really resonate with any young person reading them. <br /><br />So while ultimately I think this is a well meaning book with a well intentioned positive and empowering message I feel that... <br />(a) there were way too many issues raised in the book for it to feel realistic and that ultimately a reader could roll their eyes and just not take any of the important messages / themes of the book on board<br />(b) the writing was much too heavy handed (we've heard of the phrase mansplaining right? This is teachersplaining if there is such a thing) <br />And (c) it made me feel so old. <br /><br />Okay. I can forgive (c) because I'm certainly not the target age group for this so I've taken that into account with my rating and decided to settle on <b>three stars</b>. Otherwise it would have been two.<br /><br /><br /><i>less than 24 hours later</i><br /><br />Okay. I've been thinking about this book all day. And I'm not comfortable with my three star rating. I'm trying my best to see this as a book how a younger teen would. Try to remember what I would have thought of it at that age... But this older adult version of me is winning outright and honestly... I'm not sure the 13 year old me would have enjoyed it any more than adult me did. <br /><br />At about 1/4 the way through this I read it in a purely read to review manner garnering no enjoyment from the reading experience. I found it so heavy handed with how it was attempting to tell the reader what they should be thinking rather than letting the reader make up their own mind. <br /><br />I found that it was a book laden with too many triggering feminist issues that were easy to get riled up about rather than a book filled with the nuance and subtlety of living every day life with a feminist mindset. <br /><br />So ultimately I will award this that <b>two star</b> rating that I had originally considered. I can't in good conscience give this a rating that borders on being positive because for me, the negatives are vastly outnumbering the positive feminist message. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16080557234717034181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
