<div id="review_2038322165" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2038322165" />
    <a title="Lior" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66261781-lior"><img alt="Lior" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543889194p2/66261781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2038322165?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lior" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lior" href="/user/show/66261781-lior">Lior</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444940633" href="/book/show/35383830-moxie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66261781-lior?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038322165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5732659924836944336">(4.5)<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“This is what it means to be a feminist. Not a humanist or an equalist or whatever. But a feminist. It’s not a bad word. After today it might be my favorite word. Because really all it is is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that’s always finding ways to tell them they’re not.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>What a cute, feel good, heartwarming book! <br/><br/>I’ll be honest, I was kind of dreading this book. I was afraid it was going to be full of white, superficial, one dimensi</span>
  <span id="freeText5732659924836944336" style="display:none">(4.5)<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“This is what it means to be a feminist. Not a humanist or an equalist or whatever. But a feminist. It’s not a bad word. After today it might be my favorite word. Because really all it is is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that’s always finding ways to tell them they’re not.”</b>
</i><br /><br />What a cute, feel good, heartwarming book! <br /><br />I’ll be honest, I was kind of dreading this book. I was afraid it was going to be full of white, superficial, one dimensional, not inclusive feminism. <br />Fortunately, I was <s>mostly</s> wrong about that. This book deals with a wide array of feminist issues, from dumb sexist jokes and dress code discrimination to allies, sexual harassment and assaults. <br />All of the conflicts that came up in this book are actual conflicts that I had with myself when I started getting into feminism, and I felt that they were done in a really authentic way, and you can clearly tell that this is a process the author went through herself and it’s not just something she randomly decided to write a book about. <br /><br />I really think this book can contribute to teenage girls or anyone that’s showing interest in feminism because like I said, this book is based on real conflicts and dilemmas that “starting” feminists go through. I personally would have loved to have this book back when I was just starting to grow an interest in feminism to show me that it’s okay. <br /><br />The only criticism I have towards this book is that <b>it was a little too much tell and less show on the inclusivity.</b> I mean, yes, there are discussions in the book about the importance of inclusivity, the double oppression teenage girls from marginalized groups have to deal with, and they always make sure to make it clear that’s Moxie is for everyone, but the only real representation for that in the book is a couple black and Latina characters. It was lacking for me, I wanted to see more. <br /><br />Overall, this book is just cute and uplifting. I’d recommend it if you want to feel a little hopeful :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5732659924836944336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2050854154" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2050854154" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37692443-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593908803p2/37692443.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2050854154?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/37692443-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2050854154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4751552066952324802">I feel so honored that I have the ability to review this book early! I received this from my local bookstore and I could not be more grateful (: <br/><br/>YAY YAY YAY THIS BOOK PREACH IT! I haven't felt this empowered since I saw Wonder Woman xD<br/><br/>Ok let's start at the beginning of my journey with this book shall we? I was first exposed to Moxie when a firestorm of hype surrounded it because of a review calling this book anti male and all that. To be perfectly honest with you all, that made me slightly hesit</span>
  <span id="freeText4751552066952324802" style="display:none">I feel so honored that I have the ability to review this book early! I received this from my local bookstore and I could not be more grateful (: <br /><br />YAY YAY YAY THIS BOOK PREACH IT! I haven't felt this empowered since I saw Wonder Woman xD<br /><br />Ok let's start at the beginning of my journey with this book shall we? I was first exposed to Moxie when a firestorm of hype surrounded it because of a review calling this book anti male and all that. To be perfectly honest with you all, that made me slightly hesitant to pick up this book. I consider myself a feminist, but I didn't want to read anything... insane, you know?<br /><br />Having read it I'd like to make a little PSA: <b> THIS. BOOK. IS. NOT. ANTI. MALE!!</b> How that was even interpreted... I have no idea...but I suppose everyone is entitled to their own opinion. This book actually deals with anti male thoughts and ideas VERY WELL. It was handled in a flawless, beautiful way. Were some guys looked down simply because they were guys? Yes... but the book explains why that is in a reasonable way and those negative male feelings are pretty much resolved by the end. To me, that is the opposite of anti male. But again, everyone is entitled to believe different things. <br /><br />Okay, now that that mini rant is over let's get into more things I loved about this book. As I mentioned at the beginning. <b>THIS BOOK WAS EMPOWERING AS HELL.</b> I found myself wanting to stand up and protest right there in my living room. And I especially loved how the main characters in this book didn't start out being incredibly empowering. They slowly developed into kickass rebels and I loved that. As soon as I finished this book I ran and drew hearts and stars on my hands and it felt amazing (: (A form in which the girls protest at first). <br /><br />I also thought this book was really realistic. The sexist things that happen to these girls are 100% real and watching people naturally push back against that was really great to see. <br /><br />I think Moxie is such an important book in today's culture. It's extremely informative and deals with feminism in an excellent way. No matter who you are, whether you are a feminist or not, even if you are a girl or not, I strongly believe that everyone should read this book. I know many people who would run and hide at the word <i>feminist</i> but this story shines a light on the entire movement and explains alot. It makes the word feminist a lot less scary and a whole lot more badass. <br /><br />Now, there were a few things that I didn't absolutely love about this (hence not a full 5 stars). For one, the story dragged a bit toward the middle and I found myself having to push to get over it. Also, the characters were not my absolute favs. I think if this book was a bit longer I could have connected better with the characters much more. But, as it was, they all were sorta eh for me. But that's mostly just a me thing! <br /><br />Overall, Moxie made me laugh and tear up in joy and heartbreak and I think it will stick with me for quite sometime. What the story represents is incredibly important and I implore you to pick this one up come September. These words NEED to be read by everyone, regardless of who you are! <br /><br />Let's start a revolution ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4751552066952324802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate (GirlReading)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate (GirlReading)" href="/user/show/29599654-kate-girlreading">Kate (GirlReading)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2335960741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16993220500383561279">Moxie is a powerful story of feminism, girls supporting girls and standing up for yourself, your friends and those whose voices are hushed. It was a story full of badass, empowering, strong women and equally strong friendships pulling together to fight the good fight. The writing was easy to read, the characters were instantly likeable and the relationships, whether in a romantic, platonic or family sense, were wonderful to follow. My only criticism is that, although it is discussed in places an</span>
  <span id="freeText16993220500383561279" style="display:none">Moxie is a powerful story of feminism, girls supporting girls and standing up for yourself, your friends and those whose voices are hushed. It was a story full of badass, empowering, strong women and equally strong friendships pulling together to fight the good fight. The writing was easy to read, the characters were instantly likeable and the relationships, whether in a romantic, platonic or family sense, were wonderful to follow. My only criticism is that, although it is discussed in places and not ignored entirely, this book very much centred around one strain of feminism e.g. through that of a white, allocishet gaze. There were a few small discussions of race due to a handful of POC side characters but other than that, the feminism portrayed wasn’t wholly intersectional. However, I thoroughly enjoyed each and every page of this book and finished it feeling a sense of pride for the feminists out there, both loud and quiet, who are pushing themselves to fight for what’s right.</span>

<div id="review_2150634404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2150634404" />
    <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner"><img alt="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588471351p2/7366569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2150634404?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner">Fafa&#39;s Book Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2150634404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11443404500014418504"><a href='https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/2018/12/15/review-moxie/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Review posted on Fafa's Book Corner! </a><br/><br/>Beware spoilers ahead!<br/><br/>Trigger warning: Rape, blackmailing, harassment, bullying, slut shaming, mention of accident, sexism, misogyny, and mention of death.<br/><br/>Vivian is used to everything. She's used to behaviour of the boys. Used to all the sexist jokes, and the boy being able to get away with everything. Until Lucy transfers. Lucy is the new girl and the latest victim of Mitchell's harassment. Viv puts her foot down. Why should she and the rest of the girls ha</span>
  <span id="freeText11443404500014418504" style="display:none"><a href="https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/2018/12/15/review-moxie/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Review posted on Fafa's Book Corner! </a><br /><br />Beware spoilers ahead!<br /><br />Trigger warning: Rape, blackmailing, harassment, bullying, slut shaming, mention of accident, sexism, misogyny, and mention of death.<br /><br />Vivian is used to everything. She's used to behaviour of the boys. Used to all the sexist jokes, and the boy being able to get away with everything. Until Lucy transfers. Lucy is the new girl and the latest victim of Mitchell's harassment. Viv puts her foot down. Why should she and the rest of the girls have to deal with this?! Viv using inspiration from her mother's Riot Grrl days creates Moxie. A zine for all the females. A revolution forms. But can they hold out against the school board and most of the male population?<br /><br />I had seen Moxie on Goodreads and Twitter. I didn't care much for the synopsis. I went to the bookstore and saw it on the shelves. Out of curiosity I picked it up. I am happy to say that I enjoyed it!<br /><br />The book is written in first person limited following Vivian. There are chapter numbers. And pictures of the zines that she makes. Which could sometimes take about three pages.<br /><br />I'm really surprised that I was able to enjoy it! The synopsis read like one of those feminist books, that don't turn out that good. I can happily say that I was wrong! What I appreciated the most was the diversity! Some feminist books are actually white feminism in disguise. Which was not the case here. There were WOC and some LGBTQIA characters. And all were done so well!<br /><br />I really liked Viv! Her journey through creating Moxie was incredible. I loved that she decided to take a stand for the sake off helping her fellow women. This really is an empowering book about fantastic female friendships!<br /><br />Claudia is Viv's best friend. The two have done everything together since they were children. Their friendship is tested once the Moxie zines start coming out. Claudia like Viv has gotten used to the system. She's not quite a fan of it being questioned. Of course Claudia doesn't like the system or the general treatment, but she's used to it. This is partly why Claudia didn't like Lucy in the beginning. Lucy questioned everything and where she came from things were better. She does warm up to Lucy. And makes up with Viv.<br /><br />Lucy was such a fun character! It was nice to read about her observations on how odd the school was. She was alone in the beginning, but Moxie brought Viv and her together. Lucy and Claudia were on rocky terms in the beginning. The two do become good friends.<br /><br />Even the typical blonde cheerleader played a huge role. Viv and every other female were under the impression that Emma had a lot to gain from the system. Partly because she was pretty and didn't seem to mind the status quo. Emma turns out to be so much more! I really appreciated how the author handled women.  <br /><br />I liked Viv's relationship with her family! Her grandparents were very sweet. And her mother served for the inspiration of Moxie. Her mother's past was so cool and interesting! I love that she fought for the things she loved.<br /><br />Her and Viv do get into a bit of a rough spot. Her mother's new boyfriend plays a huge role in this. As Viv felt that her mother was changing because of said boyfriend. The two make up when Viv starts seeking her mothers advice. Viv also felt that her family wouldn't support her on Moxie. Much to her surprise they did and were proud of her.<br /><br />Viv's crush Seth also played a huge role, outside of the love interest. Seth actually caught Viv when she put out the first zine. He decided to keep it a secret. And found out cool. He became her go to person for occasional advice. There was a slow burn romance between the two which I liked!<br /><br />If it wasn't obvious with the trigger warnings this book was hard to read. There are a lot of hard subjects brought up. And while I think they were dealt with properly, it didn't make it any easier.<br /><br />It's not just the male student body that sucked, it was even the female teachers. The school board and the mentality of the town. The behaviour of these characters truly disgusted me. I spent a lot of my time reading furious at all the things that happened. Which I'm assuming was the author's intention. Kudos to the author.<br /><br />I also want to point out that I never felt that Moxie drove away male allies. Towards the end of the book the girls team up for a Moxie walkout. Seth and some of his male friends join this walkout in solidarity of the girls'. I thought that this was really powerful! Don't believe what Kirkus says.<br /><br />Overall I thoroughly enjoyed this! I highly recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11443404500014418504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2036714666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2036714666" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2036714666?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036714666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11458101033877759304">TRIGGER WARNINGS: sexual assault, misogyny<br/>REVIEW WARNING: it's a hell lot of babble<br/><br/><a href='http://ambsreads.wordpress.com/2017/09/30/moxie-by-jennifer-mathieu-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>THIS REVIEW IS ALSO ON MY BLOG</a><br/><br/>R A M B L E <br/><br/>If you ever get one book recommendation from my blog make it Moxie. Honestly, this is one of the most amazing books I have ever read. Honestly. I wish I could make everyone I know read this book. It is valuable and it is powerful. <br/><br/>These days, the word feminist is seen as a dirty word by some. It means man-hater, it means unwashed, it means venomous. Many shy away from usin</span>
  <span id="freeText11458101033877759304" style="display:none">TRIGGER WARNINGS: sexual assault, misogyny<br />REVIEW WARNING: it's a hell lot of babble<br /><br /><a href="http://ambsreads.wordpress.com/2017/09/30/moxie-by-jennifer-mathieu-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">THIS REVIEW IS ALSO ON MY BLOG</a><br /><br />R A M B L E <br /><br />If you ever get one book recommendation from my blog make it Moxie. Honestly, this is one of the most amazing books I have ever read. Honestly. I wish I could make everyone I know read this book. It is valuable and it is powerful. <br /><br />These days, the word feminist is seen as a dirty word by some. It means man-hater, it means unwashed, it means venomous. Many shy away from using the word to describe them and it sucks. I admit I have shied away from the word many times, in fear of what people will say. But now, fuck it, I'm a feminist and proud. <br /><br />There's a quote in the book that perfectly describes this and I just have to include it for everyone to read. <br /><br />"This is what it means to be a feminist. Not a humanist or an equalist or whatever. But a feminist. It's not a bad word. After today it might be my favorite word. Because really all it is is girls supporting each other and wanting to be treated like human beings in a world that's always finding ways to tell them they're not."<br />Just, wow. I am speechless about how much I love this book. I truly will be adding to my highly recommended books. It's not even that this book is aimed specifically at women, men are included throughout the narrative, proving that anyone can be a feminist. Something that needs to be known in a world (especially the Internet world) where it is laughed at and mocked.  <br /><br />ALSO! THERE WERE SO MANY TALL GIRLS. Y'ALL DON'T KNOW HAPPY THIS MAKES ME. BEING 5'11 I BARELY SEE GIRLS CLOSE TO MY HEIGHT BUT VIVIAN IS 5'10 AND LUCY IS EVEN TALLER!!!!!<br /><br />P L O T <br /><br />The plot centres around Vivian and her urge to do something in her school which is run by misogynistic men where boys are able to get away with absolutely everything. It is the typical school where girls are made to feel as if they are distracting boys purely by wearing a singlet. <br /><br />I hate to say it, but my high school was pretty similar to this. A friend of mine was cornered by a boy and he tried to force himself on her. She thankfully got away and went straight to the principal. She was told she had been asking for it and it was her fault she wore the school uniform like she did. The guy later tried to go after my little sister and my friend moved to the other side of the country. Basically, my school was filled with these stereotypical guys who think they can do anything they want because they're a gift to all us mere female peasants (kill me). <br /><br />Back to Moxie, Vivian becomes inspired after going through a box of her mum's belongings from her youth. Her mum had been incredibly active in the feminist movement within her era, something which gives Vivian the inspiration to create a zine (not a newsletter) which will inspire the girls at her high school. <br /><br />She never expects this particular zine to gain growth and popularity. Soon a lot of girls within her high school are becoming Moxie girls and fighting back against the oppression. It was honestly incredible and I can't fault much about this book (apart from a few careless mentions of the word depression). The diverse cast pushes the plot forward and it is honestly just so inspiring. <br /><br />Even when the romance is introduced to the novel the aspect of girl power doesn't take a back seat. Vivian continues on her path and does not become love struck (okay, she does a little), something I loved. Also, the amazing girl friendships within. I always want more powerful friendships between girls in fiction and this book delivered tenfold. The relationship between Vivian and Lucy kind of reminded me of me and my best friend. I just love it so much. There was also an incredible family dynamic between Viv and her mum. It was very realistic for someone who's mum is her best friend. <br /><br />C H A R A C T E R S <br /><br />#V I V I A N <br /><br />Vivian has to be one of the most impressive and amazing main characters I have ever read. I have read some pretty incredible main characters, including Starr from THUG, but Vivian is up there. Way up there. <br /><br />Being a notorious good girl Viv doesn't do a lot. She studies, visits her friends and doesn't get in trouble. However, she wants to make a change in her school. She wants to make the careless "make a sandwich" and other ridiculous comments stop. Doing this she decides to create a zine, which leads to her getting her first boyfriend and discovering amazing new friends in her school. It was just incredible. I have no other words. <br /><br />The relationships that develop and are shown are in no way forced. They are so damn real it almost felt I was reading about a friend group I had. I just have no words. Vivian is such a great main character and her growth is amazing. I'm just so speechless. <br /><br />The other cast of characters are incredible. From Emma, Lucy, Claudia, Seth and everyone else (there are so many) it is amazing how they all come together in this story to spread one message. <br /><br />O V E R A L L <br /><br />Overall, one of the most amazing books I know I'll read this year. I truly, truly, can't recommend this enough. Buy this now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11458101033877759304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2550398373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2550398373" />
    <a title="Faye*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11652288-faye"><img alt="Faye*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508097472p2/11652288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2550398373?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye*" href="/user/show/11652288-faye">Faye*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444940633" href="/book/show/35383830-moxie">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2550398373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11532216569482501937">YES TO THIS BOOK!<br/><br/>Sexism exists. Girls and women feel unsafe, belittled, objectified, and humiliated every day, even in so-called “first world” countries, where we’re supposedly so far ahead and women have exactly the same rights and opportunities as men. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524036258ra/25395002.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>+ I have lived a very sheltered life so far (and I’m very grateful for it, don’t worry). If there is one thing that this book accomplished it’s reminding me of how lucky I’ve been, and how different and how unfair the world is for so many other </span>
  <span id="freeText11532216569482501937" style="display:none">YES TO THIS BOOK!<br><br>Sexism exists. Girls and women feel unsafe, belittled, objectified, and humiliated every day, even in so-called “first world” countries, where we’re supposedly so far ahead and women have exactly the same rights and opportunities as men. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524036258ra/25395002.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>+ I have lived a very sheltered life so far (and I’m very grateful for it, don’t worry). If there is one thing that this book accomplished it’s reminding me of how lucky I’ve been, and how different and how unfair the world is for so many other girls, even ones that are lucky enough to be able to go to school and live pretty sheltered lives themselves. Even if many (though not all) of the things that happen in this book are comparatively "little" or "mild" compared to what some girls and women have to endure, all these smaller and bigger stings make those girls uncomfortable. They don't feel safe at their school and like they are not allowed to take up space there. This is why this book is so important because these "little" things matter.<br><br>+ I loved the story around Vivian and her friends, the way they learned to stand up for themselves, unsure at first but more and more confident. Even though this isn’t a page turner in the usual sense, I found myself engrossed in the story, looking forward to the next Moxie edition, curious to see what the girls were going to come up with next. <br><br>+ Loved the character growth in this story. Watching Vivian, Claudia, Seth, and all the others learn and grow together was beautiful to see. <br><br>+ Also loved how Moxie created this bond between the girls, how they started supporting each other, and even reviving old friendships. We need to see more female friendships and girls supporting girls, especially in books for younger readers. <br><br><br>- As for the negatives, this sometimes read like a bad dystopian to me. It may be because I don’t live in the U.S. but reading this story about this football-crazed town where arbitrary dress codes for girls are enforced, and the football players get away with literally everything in such a blatant way made it seem rather black and white to me. I’m probably being naïve but please tell me that high schools like this don’t actually exist. I really want to believe that Jennifer Mathieu exaggerated things to make her book more impactful and the unfairness more tangible for the reader, especially for younger ones. If she did, I think it was overdone and, as I said, very black-and-white. If she didn’t, well… I guess you already know what I think.<br><br>- Although I loved that this was such a quick and easy read, the informal language sometimes was a bit too much for me. I know that teenagers today, like, totally talk like that. And I get that it makes this book, like, totally relatable, which is, like, totally important. But on the other hand, it totally made me, like, cringe or whatever to, like, see this printed because I feel like it totally shouldn’t be encouraged. If you, like, know what I mean or whatever. <br>Also, this is an actual quote from the book: “Seth Acosta is not ho hum or meh or vanilla or blah. He’s a stone fox.” I mean, what?<br><br>- Why are there never any adults in these books that the protagonists can actually confide in? You know the ones, who don't punish the entire class when the school's biggest asshole speaks out of turn? Or the parents, who are not constantly out working so our protagonist can conveniently create her zines in secret and hang out with her boyfriend all the time? <br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31529984-eli" rel="nofollow noopener">Eli</a>!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538653648ra/26399331.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11532216569482501937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2130180479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2130180479" />
    <a title="TJL" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40284117-tjl"><img alt="TJL" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426450509p2/40284117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2130180479?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TJL" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TJL" href="/user/show/40284117-tjl">TJL</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=i-wanted-to-slap-the-main-character">i-wanted-to-slap-the-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=irritating-sexism-preaching">irritating-sexism-preaching</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=characters-you-love-to-hate">characters-you-love-to-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=main-character-is-a-brat">main-character-is-a-brat</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=main-character-is-a-hypocrite">main-character-is-a-hypocrite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=i-am-actually-seething-with-rage">i-am-actually-seething-with-rage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=this-book-made-me-angry">this-book-made-me-angry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=main-character-is-a-twit">main-character-is-a-twit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40284117-tjl?shelf=preachy-af">preachy-af</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2130180479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5130701998241506285">I knew exactly what I was getting into.<br/><br/>I knew that.<br/><br/>I knew this book was going to be "Why Feminism is DA BEST THING EVAR and Boys Are Icky Yucky Sexist Dudebro Pigs". I knew that. <br/><br/>So why did I decide to read it?<br/><br/>Fuck if I know. I guess I just like watching train-wrecks. <br/><br/>So let me just outline some highlights- in no particular order- with a reminder that I am a woman, and therefore are especially fucking bothered by some of this shit:<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[1. Viv is so sensitive that she loses her shit ove</span></span>
  <span id="freeText5130701998241506285" style="display:none">I knew exactly what I was getting into.<br /><br />I knew that.<br /><br />I knew this book was going to be "Why Feminism is DA BEST THING EVAR and Boys Are Icky Yucky Sexist Dudebro Pigs". I knew that. <br /><br />So why did I decide to read it?<br /><br />Fuck if I know. I guess I just like watching train-wrecks. <br /><br />So let me just outline some highlights- in no particular order- with a reminder that I am a woman, and therefore are especially fucking bothered by some of this shit:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. Viv is so sensitive that she loses her shit over a t-shirt that says "great legs, when do they open?" Good to know women are so sensitive that we can't keep our heads together over a shirt. <br /><br />I'm curious, Viv, why is the shirt gross? It's gender-neutral. There's no indicator whether or not its referring to a man's legs or a woman's. It's sexual innuendo- I see worse in the WOMEN'S bathrooms at my workplace. But I'm not surprised that Viv fantasizes about complaining about his shirt, or about cutting it up, or who basically ends up GOING TO THE NURSE BECAUSE IT MAKES HER FEEL SICK- this entire book is pretty much Example 1 of why I can't fucking deal with feminism, namely that they're a hypersensitive bunch that loses their minds over little things like writing on a goddamn t-shirt.<br /><br />It's a <i>shirt</i>. A shirt that's inappropriate for school, but a shirt nevertheless. Toughen the <i>fuck</i> up and find a better hill to die on, for God's sake. <br /><br />2. Male Football Player Students saying "make me a sandwich" whenever a female student speaks up in class. Dear Jesus- I was torn between puking and laughing hysterically. This is a published book, in a bookstore, that costs money. It's basically a Tumblrite's "AND THEN THE WHOLE BUS CLAPPED" story that you have to spend money to read (unless, like me, you got it from a library). <br /><br />Could you have gone with a more stereotypical depiction? I've ranted and raved about this idiotic trope, Football Players are Stupid Sexist Dudebros, more times than I can count. How very new and original and not at all, in itself, a sexist depiction that's been around for decades. Am I supposed to be impressed by the fact that the football players are the bad guys here? <br /><br />This is so unoriginal it's <i>painful</i>.<br /><br />But let's be real: If this were a book that didn't engage in ridiculous hyperbole and exaggeration then the main character (and by association, the audience) MIGHT be forced to admit that the male of the species is not as evil as they want to believe- and that, perhaps, some women and girls are railing against a beast that is far less common than they think it is. <br /><br />3. The author recommends "Feministing" as one of her "Feminist" blog resources. Feministing, if you aren't familiar with it, was founded by Jessica Valenti; a true paragon of maturity who is perhaps best recognized from a photo circulating the internet of her, on the beach, wearing a "I bathe in male tears" sweatshirt. And oh, while we're at it, let's have some <i>quotes</i> from Miss Valenti:<br /><br /><blockquote>Men who claim to be genuinely worried about man-hating or “misandry” are grasping at straws, and searching for a victim status that simply doesn’t exist. <b>Guys are still doing pretty well, so let us have our “man-hating” fun while you go on ruling the world.</b></blockquote><br /><br />*Sniffs* Ah, smell that equality! Men should just sit back and take irrational hatred from women because they deserve it! And that's just the tip of the ice-berg: Valenti's gone on record numerous times stating, more or less, that women have no right to oppose or refuse the title of "Feminist"- and you DEFINITELY don't have the right to criticize the feminist movement and its participants. If you're not a feminist, then you should just <a href="https://ima-fuckingt4ble.tumblr.com/post/120697106636/why-do-you-dislike-feminism-so-much-because" rel="nofollow noopener">hand back your right to vote, your anti-rape laws, and basically all your rights.</a><br /><br />Because "I did something nice for you, so you're not allowed to criticize me or leave me" is TOTALLY NOT THE ABUSER 101 TAGLINE. <br /><br />That's who the author has just recommended you go to for your Feminist education, kids. Remember that. <i>Remember that</i>. <br /><br />4. Because Seth is a guy, he will <i>never know what it is to walk down the hall and be judged for his appearance.</i> I think the most insulting part of this claim, made by Viv later in the book, is the assumption that girls and ONLY GIRLS have beauty standards- because obviously overweight guys with neckbeards are never, ever mocked. Ever. ESPECIALLY not on the internet! And pencil-thin dudes with acne and glasses? Oh God, of COURSE nobody ever calls them weedy nerds- certainly never <i>girls</i>. <br /><br />Do I- I mean, I'm assuming whoever reads this has at least half a fucking brain, you KNOW that's not true, right? That men are regularly judged on their appearance and held to standards, right? The only difference is that when THEY complain about it, the feminist movement tells them to shut up because "DA WOMEN HAVE IT WORSE".<br /><br />5. It turns out the Big Bad Evil Sexist Principal wasn't JUST a Big Bad Sexist- he was literally stealing money from GIRLS SPORTS to give it to FOOTBALL, which is a BOYS SPORT. As in, LITERALLY STEALING MONEY FROM THE GIRLS TO GIVE TO THE BOYS.<br /><br />I cannot make this up. It wasn't enough for the football players to be the bad guys- we had to have the girls be just the BIGGEST ULTIMATE VICTIMS OF THE SCHOOL SYSTEM. <br /><br />6. That <i>dress-code bullshit.</i>. <br /><br />This was an exaggeration of the usual idiotic, petty dress-code argument I hear from Tumblr feminists on a regular goddamn basis, because apparently the following is too hard to comprehend:<br /><br />Girls have more variety of dress than boys.<br /><br />Girls have more revealing clothing available [edit: THAN] boys: How often do you see boys wearing tank-tops with spaghetti straps? How often do you see boys wearing shorts that don't reach to mid-thigh? How often do you see boys wearing shirts that reveal too much of his chest? WHEN WAS THE LAST TIME YOU SAW A BOY WEARING A MINI-SKIRT??<br /><br />YOU GENERALLY <b>DON'T</b>, because that's not how male fashion, at the moment, WORKS. <br /><br /><b>THAT'S WHY THEY FOCUS ON GIRLS MORE THAN BOYS.<br /><br /><i>GIRLS HAVE MORE CHOICES THAN BOYS FASHION-WISE.</i></b><br /><br />What happened in this book was a strawman argument: It was presenting a <i>completely unrealistic</i> scenario to whine, OVERALL, about how sexist dress-codes are. I have ZERO tolerance for this immature, petty argument and the whiny little girls who complain about how "sexist" it is that they can't wear a mini-skirt at school or wear disturbingly revealing shirts. <br /><br />AGAIN: <i>PICK A BETTER HILL TO DIE ON</i>. <br /><br />6. And this part. <i>This part</i>. <br /><br /><blockquote>Viv: "He'll never know how scary and crazy-making it is to feel like you belong to some big Boy Monster that decides it can grab you and touch you and rank you whenever and however it wants."</blockquote><br /><br />And THIS PART<br /><br /><blockquote>Seth: "But I promise that from now on I'm going to try to listen better about the stuff I <b>can't totally understand because I'm a guy</b>."<br /><br />Viv: "See, there you go, You say you're not perfect, <b>but that answer makes me think you're pretty close</b>."</blockquote><br /><br />I've been sarcastic up until this point, but let me get <i>deadly</i> fucking serious with you right now.<br /><br />I have no tolerance for this kind of feminism.<br /><br />Zero. Tolerance.<br /><br />It promotes a victimhood mentality. It promotes a "The Big Bad Corrupt Menz are out to get us Poor Defenseless and Pure Women. We are literally always at the mercy of the ebil menz" mentality. <br /><br />I have seen young women on Tumblr remark about how they feel they "literally can't go out at night" because The Men will assault them and rape them and kill them. They claim to be strong, empowered women who will KICK YOUR ASS, BRO, but they whine and bitch and wail about how big and bad and <i>scary</i> the men are, and expect everyone to kowtow to their fear. <br /><br />The second set of quotes almost gave me an aneurysm, because at the heart of it, that's the sort of feminism this book promotes: It's the kind of feminism that claims to want "equality of the genders" but then demands that men shut up and let women talk. This is not the sort of feminism that encourages a dialogue- at heart, it's basically, "Women can make all the declarations, and if the men debate this or disagree with us, They Just Don't Get It because they're Not Women." <br /><br />This entire goddamn book was a stark, slap-in-the-face reminder of why I am firmly Not a Feminist. The author made every scenario in this book into a disgusting strawman exaggeration: The Evil Rapist Football Dudebros are ruling our Sexist School System That Hates Young Women and Wants Us All to Just Sit Back and Shut Up". <br /><br />This is every feminist fear-tactic in one book: The men are out to get you, especially the high school football players. <br /><br />The world is an evil, sexist cesspit that won't let you dress the way you want because you're a girl. <br /><br />Girls are the eternal victims of the world and boys will just never understaaaaand us. <br /><br />And you can absolutely claim to be empowered despite being such a delicate flower that you lose your shit over a stupid t-shirt that a boy wears. <br /><br />I'm an adult, and this is a movement AND BOOK that caters to a brand of feminism practiced by petty children. I'm frankly disgusted beyond belief at how willingly and happily this book embraces immature feminist rhetoric- it's completely lacking in self-awareness. <br /><br />Your main character has to go home with a stomachache because a boy wore a t-shirt that says "Nice Legs, when do they open?" You are SO fucking delicate that you can't handle words on a SHIRT? <br /><br />THAT is our hero? <br /><br />tl;dr: This book was basically a cornfield full of petty, whiny, immature, Feminist Straw(wo)men and you'd be better off reading a radfem's tumblr blog; same information, and you don't have to pay jack-shit for it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="5130701998241506285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2067468837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067468837" />
    <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books"><img alt="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415550632p2/5892196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067468837?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books">Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=2019-netgalley-challenge">2019-netgalley-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067468837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15402478783007625782">This review can also be found at <a href='https://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life in Books</a>.<br/><br/>I really ended up enjoying this book! This was a review book that completely slipped through the cracks and was left to sit somewhat forgotten. By the time I pulled it out of the pile, I didn't completely remember why I had been drawn to it in the first place. I wasn't too far into the book when I realized just how good this story really was and I had a fantastic time with it.<br/><br/>It has been a long time since I was a teenager or went to </span>
  <span id="freeText15402478783007625782" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="https://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life in Books</a>.<br /><br />I really ended up enjoying this book! This was a review book that completely slipped through the cracks and was left to sit somewhat forgotten. By the time I pulled it out of the pile, I didn't completely remember why I had been drawn to it in the first place. I wasn't too far into the book when I realized just how good this story really was and I had a fantastic time with it.<br /><br />It has been a long time since I was a teenager or went to high school. A very long time. My youngest daughter is currently finishing up her final year of high school and my oldest is a young adult so I have lived with teenagers for quite a few years so I feel like I know what they are like and I thought that this book was filled with realistic teenagers which is one of the things that I really really enjoyed about it.<br /><br />I wish that the things that happen at Vivian's high school during the course of this book didn't happen. I know that they happened when I was in school and I don't think it is too much of a stretch to think that they still happen quite often in certain areas. I was mad. I was disappointed. And I was disappointed. How could the adults let these things happen and not speak up? How was it that none of the parents of daughters from the school were demanding change? The one thing that I would have loved to see happen in this book would be for Vivian, or one of her friends, to tell the adult in their life exactly what was going on. <br /><br />These girls didn't let others fight their battles though. Vivian sparks a movement that eventually works its way across her school. I was so happy to see these girls stand up and fight the things that were wrong together. It was a very uplifting message about how change can happen if you get enough people to stand up with you. <br /><br />I listened to the audiobook version of this book which turned out to be a fantastic choice because Suzy Jackson did a wonderful job with the story. She really was the voice of Vivian and I thought that she did was able to bring this story to life. All of the character voices were really well done and I had no problems listening to this book for hours at a time.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to others. I had a great time watching this wonderful group of characters fight for a cause that was easy to get behind. I look forward to reading more of Jennifer Mathieu's work in the future.<br /><br /><i>I received a digital review copy of this book from Macmillan Children's Publishing Group via NetGalley and borrowed a copy of the audiobook from my local library.</i><br /><br /><b>Initial Thoughts</b><br />Such a good story! This was a story about girls standing up for themselves, for what is right, and for each other. It makes me mad that we live in a world where treating certain people differently than others still happens but I love the fact that people are working to make a change. I listened to the audiobook and thought that the narrator did a fantastic job with the story.</span>

          <a title="Reading By Moonlight Book Club " class="actionLink" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/20004773-august-2019-book-announcement">Reading By Moonli...:</a>
        </b>
      
			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/20004773-august-2019-book-announcement">August 2019 Book Announcement </a>

	<tr>
		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gm7efX04H2bDfpe57zMHkdAutjOKm/RxAHhbpQ8P8SQBP6b7Fwbsbcds8kuAp1Un4GwlBDuJARDZZUglNNnQlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wf3wpqbE46xjedA4Q6ttYHRU4qpxOSeNIWRzYKYZdODarIggzPoQp2drtcosPz/WRBZxncAr0uz4eWDgnc9VUQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer18060711882527804146">I'm a high school English teacher, writer, wife, and mom who writes books for and about young adults. My novels include MOXIE, THE TRUTH ABOUT ALICE, DEVOTED, and AFTERWARD.<br/><br/>My fifth novel, THE LIARS OF MARIPOSA ISLAND, will be out in September 2019. <br/><br/>My novel MOXIE will soon be a movie for Netflix directed by none other than Amy Poehler!   <span id="freeText18060711882527804146" style="display:none">I'm a high school English teacher, writer, wife, and mom who writes books for and about young adults. My novels include MOXIE, THE TRUTH ABOUT ALICE, DEVOTED, and AFTERWARD.<br /><br />My fifth novel, THE LIARS OF MARIPOSA ISLAND, will be out in September 2019. <br /><br />My novel MOXIE will soon be a movie for Netflix directed by none other than Amy Poehler! It has a special Tumblr I adore that you can check out at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.moxiegirlsfightback.com">www.moxiegirlsfightback.com</a>! <br /><br />All my novels are published by Roaring Brook Press/Macmillan.<br /><br />My favorite things include chocolate, pepperoni pizza, and this super hilarious 1980s sitcom about four retired women called The Golden Girls. I can basically quote every episode.<br /><br />I live in Texas with my husband, son, and dog. <br /><br />When it comes to what I read, I love realistic young adult fiction (duh), creative nonfiction, super scandalous tell-all memoirs and unauthorized biographies, and basically anything that hooks me on the first page.<br /></span>
